[1]The Tinellbian Languages Dictionary
[2]About
[d introduction]
This dictionary aims to describe all the vocabulary items of the twenty Tinellbian languages, consisting of High Lulani and its descendants. In addition, miscellaneous English neologisms have been added, including proper nouns.
[/d]
[d javascript]
[d introduction]
[2]Searching
The search box at the bottom of each page allows one to proceed directly to any dictionary entry. Contrariwise, the search box in the navigation pane runs a general search of the site.

[1]-&#x294;a
[2]High Lulani
[3]<high-lulani>;a</high-lulani>
[4]<ipa><a href="http://grammar.tinellb.com/highlulani/phonology/index.html">/&#x294;.j&#x259;/</a></ipa>
[5]particle <div class="definition"><em>(indicates emphasis)</em></div>
[6]Usage Notes
Placed at the end of greetings and valedictions.
Often elided, moving the stress of the last word to the final syllable.
[6]Example

[e]<a href="../d/da.html#highlulani">da</a>-<a href="../q/qa.html#highlulani">qa</a> <a href="../a/'ala.html#highlulani">&rsquo;ala</a>
[e]<em>water-gen heat</em>
[e]&ldquo;the heat of the water&rdquo;[/d]
[5]<a href="http://grammar.tinellb.com/highlulani/morphology/nouns/index.html#abstractnoun">abstract</a> stem count <a href="http://grammar.tinellb.com/highlulani/morphology/nouns/index.html">noun</a> <div class="definition">temperature degree</div>
[6]Notes*
This temperature scale is set with <strong>0</strong> <em>0</em> at absolute zero, and <strong>495</strong> <em>230</em> at the triple point of water.
In ordinary use, temperatures between <strong>450</strong> <em>200</em> and <strong>675</strong> <em>300</em> are given without the hundreds place.
<p class="note">*Numbers in <strong>bold</strong> are in decimal, numbers in <em>italics</em> are in balanced <a href="../s/sesquidecimal.html#highlulani">sesquidecimal</a>.</p>&date=20180327--------------------------------------------------2

[1]bitta
[2]High Lulani
[3]<high-lulani>B;t</high-lulani>
[4]<ipa><a href="http://grammar.tinellb.com/highlulani/phonology/index.html">/&#x2c8;bit.t&#x259;/</a></ipa>
[5]<a href="http://grammar.tinellb.com/highlulani/morphology/nouns/index.html#inanimatenoun">inanimate</a> stem <a href="http://grammar.tinellb.com/highlulani/morphology/nouns/index.html">noun</a> <div class="definition">time</div>
[6]Definition
the two temporal dimensions
[6]Notes
The first dimension of time is subjective: a person&rsquo;s birth is <em>before</em> their death.
The second dimension is objective: if one time-travels into the past, then one&rsquo;s death may well be <em>upstream</em> of one&rsquo;s birth.

[6]Notes

[1]gingla
[2]English
[3]
[4]<ipa>/&#x2c8;gi&#x14b;.gl&#x259;/</ipa>
[5]abstract stem noun <div class="definition">planes of existence; ghostly realms</div>
[6]Definition
there are four ginglaic dimensions. These correspond to the seven planes in some esoteric systems, or to otherworldly realms, <em>i.e.:</em> in order to explain paranormal events.
[6]Notes
<a href="../x/xaraduluri.html">Xaraduluri</a> are capable of moving through <em>gingla</em>
